<div id="review_2443169909" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2443169909" />
    <a title="Tom Quinn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31467977-tom-quinn"><img alt="Tom Quinn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574458226p2/31467977.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2443169909?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tom Quinn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tom Quinn" href="/user/show/31467977-tom-quinn">Tom Quinn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title=" 9783442545698" href="/book/show/835386.Lullaby">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2443169909" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3084486054961357585">Love him or hate him, you must admit: Chuck Palahniuk is always inventive. Sometimes it's to the point of being gimmicky (<i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4601396-pygmy?ac=1&from_search=true' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pygmy</a>
</i>, anyone?) but original ideas and memorable execution like those displayed in <i>Lullaby</i> are among the stronger stuff you'll find in American pop fiction of the early millennium. Plus Palahniuk is a regular workhorse of a writer, having put out a new title every few years for the better part of two decades. Will they all be remembered in years to come? Doubtful. But he </span>
  <span id="freeText3084486054961357585" style="display:none">Love him or hate him, you must admit: Chuck Palahniuk is always inventive. Sometimes it's to the point of being gimmicky (<i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4601396-pygmy?ac=1&amp;from_search=true" rel="nofollow noopener">Pygmy</a>
</i>, anyone?) but original ideas and memorable execution like those displayed in <i>Lullaby</i> are among the stronger stuff you'll find in American pop fiction of the early millennium. Plus Palahniuk is a regular workhorse of a writer, having put out a new title every few years for the better part of two decades. Will they all be remembered in years to come? Doubtful. But he entertains, dang it, and sometimes that's all we're looking for in a book.<br /><br />4 stars out of 5. I like this one of his better than most because you can read it symbolically (not very hard to do since he's pretty overt with his message) but it's also just a fast-paced supernatural thriller with a few twists that I didn't see coming.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3084486054961357585" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_46537723" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/46537723" />
    <a title="Dana Cordelia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1548009-dana-cordelia"><img alt="Dana Cordelia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1358296419p2/1548009.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/46537723?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dana Cordelia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dana Cordelia" href="/user/show/1548009-dana-cordelia">Dana Cordelia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1548009-dana-cordelia?shelf=must-read">must-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer46537723" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2813429744498838035">My interest in Palahniuk was selfish: since suffering the loss of a loved one, experiencing a mental breakdown at PDX airport and, two days later, being terminated from my hellish job and thrown blindly into unemployment with no health insurance, no savings and a laundry list of neurological pills that needed popping (prescribing, and purchasing, too...) I was desperate for a distraction. <br/><br/>This book is aaaaallllllll about the distraction, the noise, and the general clusterfuck that spins on aroun</span>
  <span id="freeText2813429744498838035" style="display:none">My interest in Palahniuk was selfish: since suffering the loss of a loved one, experiencing a mental breakdown at PDX airport and, two days later, being terminated from my hellish job and thrown blindly into unemployment with no health insurance, no savings and a laundry list of neurological pills that needed popping (prescribing, and purchasing, too...) I was desperate for a distraction. <br /><br />This book is aaaaallllllll about the distraction, the noise, and the general clusterfuck that spins on around us, preventing us from thinking. It's characterized as the good and the bad; honestly, how much do you really want to focus on your life when your life seems so hopeless and backwards?<br /><br />"Lullaby" centers around a reporter's discovery and subsequent utilization of a "culling song," or a poem recited to individuals to put them to sleep, put them out of their misery...basically you direct the words to them, and they die. Someone has placed the poem in a book of verses from around the world, and parents are reading it to their babies, and a mysterious surge in SIDS deaths has compelled the reporter to find the connection.<br /><br />The song is the connection: and, now that he knows, he holds the power of life and death over the cacophonous world around him.<br />Call it how you see it: in some ways this book is about a man's moral struggle with the power he finds. In some ways, a road trip, finding copies of the book with cohorts who all want something else from the grimoire from which the poem originated. In others, it's about the choices set before them when the grail (of sorts) is found. Save the world by healing and teaching and making positive changes? Rule the world by killing off your enemies and empowering your allies? Turn everything into ashes and dust, and let the world begin again? Or...<br /><br />I can't recommend it highly enough. On a personal note, I'm racked with the tearful relief that there is someone in this world sicker than I am. I sincerely enjoyed this book. I was engrossed, I was impressed, I'll likely read it again. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2813429744498838035" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_648909914" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/648909914" />
    <a title="Luis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14022277-luis"><img alt="Luis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1405055883p2/14022277.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/648909914?book_show_action=true">Jun 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Luis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Luis" href="/user/show/14022277-luis">Luis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780385722193" href="/book/show/457015.Lullaby">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14022277-luis?shelf=reread">reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14022277-luis?shelf=chuck-palahniuk">chuck-palahniuk</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer648909914" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13618821494324722524">How words can be so powerful. How you are never sure whether the life you're having is the life you want or the life you've been trained to want. How you would come to think that your mind is never ever yours alone. How they--from God to tv commercials--control your thoughts for you. To occupy you so you won't be able to have the time to think about things. So you won't have time to actually rebel.<br/><br/><blockquote>Experts in ancient Greek culture say that people back then didn't see their thoughts as belonging t</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText13618821494324722524" style="display:none">How words can be so powerful. How you are never sure whether the life you're having is the life you want or the life you've been trained to want. How you would come to think that your mind is never ever yours alone. How they--from God to tv commercials--control your thoughts for you. To occupy you so you won't be able to have the time to think about things. So you won't have time to actually rebel.<br /><br /><blockquote>Experts in ancient Greek culture say that people back then didn't see their thoughts as belonging to them. When ancient Greeks had a thought, it occurred to them as a god or goddess giving an order. Apollo was telling them to be brave. Athena was telling them to fall in love. <br /><br />Now people hear a commercial for sour cream potato chips and rush out to buy, but now they call this free will.<br />At least the ancient Greeks were being honest.</blockquote><br /><br /><i>Lullaby</i>, so far in my Chuck reads, is Chuck's most direct attack to the idea of God. And to society wanting to control you. It's also kind of a light read when it comes to Chuck's way of narrating. It isn't spilling too much repetitive sentences. (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/842995.Diary" title="Diary by Chuck Palahniuk" rel="nofollow noopener">Diary</a> on the other hand IS FULL of repetitions). And our hero, Carl Streator, isn't much of a nihilist in the beginning.<br /><br /><blockquote>Big Brother isn’t watching. He’s singing and dancing. He’s pulling rabbits out of a hat. Big Brother’s busy holding your attention every moment you’re awake. He’s making sure you’re always distracted. He’s making sure you’re fully absorbed.</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="13618821494324722524" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_422905391" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/422905391" />
    <a title="Rayna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12459424-rayna"><img alt="Rayna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499830159p2/12459424.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/422905391?book_show_action=true">Sep 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rayna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rayna" href="/user/show/12459424-rayna">Rayna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12459424-rayna?shelf=2012">2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer422905391" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer478278956457394478">I recently stated to a friend that I had serious reservations about reading a Chuck Palahniuk novel. I, like many, do not like to be typecast into certain roles. Due to my age, interests, and lets just admit it, "quirks," I am a perfect candidate for membership in the Chuck Palahniuk fan club. Yet, for the majority of my adult life thus far I have been fighting the urge to, "drink the kool-aid," my scenester peers seem to enjoy so much. How very scenester of me, right? I mean come on, I gave the</span>
  <span id="freeText478278956457394478" style="display:none">I recently stated to a friend that I had serious reservations about reading a Chuck Palahniuk novel. I, like many, do not like to be typecast into certain roles. Due to my age, interests, and lets just admit it, "quirks," I am a perfect candidate for membership in the Chuck Palahniuk fan club. Yet, for the majority of my adult life thus far I have been fighting the urge to, "drink the kool-aid," my scenester peers seem to enjoy so much. How very scenester of me, right? I mean come on, I gave the first, "Twilight," installment a chance. While this is not a good arguement to support ANYTHING it was convincing enough for me to try, "Chuck P."<br />This being said, I really enjoyed the novel, "Lullaby." Serve me some of that kool-aid cause it is tasty! <br />In short, this novel introduces a reader to the concept of a, "culling song." A chant that when spoken is lethal to whoever is listening. The plot revolves around a circle of amusing quirky characters, all fighting for power over this supernatural anomaly. I found the majority of this book to be extremely entertaining. "Lullaby," was the perfect representation of outlandish human behavior, brought on by great supernatural power. What's the line, "absolute power corrupts absolutely?"<br />In truth, the only complaint I had regarding, "Lullaby," was I found Chuck Palahniuk's writing a little, "preachy," at times. As you may guess, this book brought up a "myriad" of ethical questions. As a reader, I found Chuck Palahniuk repeatedly drilling them into my brain. In my opinion, if a reader is not aware enough to identify these questions for themselves, a Chuck Palahniuk book is probably dangerous in their hands.<br />All this being said, you will most likely find me in the future "slugging" down a latte, blasting the latest Interpol album, with a Chuck Palahniuk book in my hand. </span>
  <a data-text-id="478278956457394478" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('jl9IrapFr4MYChm8ENUBqwZOIZPeQHkMO3f8NRvtrzW0eSF/ERtm678hrd3nIAt00BHGWxDN92tgCbqE1q5drw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('FfA/oEdz8epTYJWK1+Wop+Dp3ztQIAZItihoUe9HeBEv1lZy/C04gvRLIesgEKJ4NrY4856tiC/tVi7gIgSKiw==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/2546.Chuck_Palahniuk">About Chuck Palahniuk</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/2546.Chuck_Palahniuk"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1391203076p3/2546.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/2546.Chuck_Palahniuk">Chuck Palahniuk
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
124,902
followers
</div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17934591094866876287">Written in stolen moments under truck chassis and on park benches to a soundtrack of The Downward Spiral and Pablo Honey, <i>Fight Club</i> came into existence. The adaptation of <i>Fight Club</i> was a flop at the box office, but achieved cult status on DVD. The film’s popularity drove sales of the novel. Chuck put out two novels in 1999, <i>Survivor</i> and <i>Invisible Monsters</i>. <i>Choke</i>, published in 2001, became Chuck’</span>
  <span id="freeText17934591094866876287" style="display:none">Written in stolen moments under truck chassis and on park benches to a soundtrack of The Downward Spiral and Pablo Honey, <i>Fight Club</i> came into existence. The adaptation of <i>Fight Club</i> was a flop at the box office, but achieved cult status on DVD. The film’s popularity drove sales of the novel. Chuck put out two novels in 1999, <i>Survivor</i> and <i>Invisible Monsters</i>. <i>Choke</i>, published in 2001, became Chuck’s first New York Times bestseller. Chuck’s work has always been infused with personal experience, and his next novel, <i>Lullaby</i>, was no exception. Chuck credits writing <i>Lullaby</i> with helping him cope with the tragic death of his father. <i>Diary</i> and the non-fiction guide to Portland, <i>Fugitives and Refugees</i>, were released in 2003. While on the road in support of <i>Diary</i>, Chuck began reading a short story entitled 'Guts,' which would eventually become part of the novel <i>Haunted</i>.<br /><br />In the years that followed, he continued to write, publishing the bestselling <i>Rant, Snuff, Pygmy, Tell-All, a 'remix' of Invisible Monsters, Damned</i>, and most recently, <i>Doomed</i>. <br /><br />Chuck also enjoys giving back to his fans, and teaching the art of storytelling has been an important part of that. In 2004, Chuck began submitting essays to ChuckPalahniuk.net on the craft of writing. These were 'How To' pieces, straight out of Chuck's personal bag of tricks, based on the tenants of minimalism he learned from Tom Spanbauer. Every month, a “Homework Assignment” would accompany the lesson, so Workshop members could apply what they had learned. (all 36 of these essays can currently be found on The Cult's sister-site, LitReactor.com).<br /><br />Then, in 2009, Chuck increased his involvement by committing to read and review a selection of fan-written stories each month. The best stories are currently set to be published in <i>Burnt Tongues</i>, a forthcoming anthology, with an introduction written by Chuck himself. <br /><br />His next novel, <i>Beautiful You</i>, is due out in October 2014.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17934591094866876287" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
